Slaughter Tax Questioned Yesterday 96

News from Both Government and Business Sides

Meat Industry Association Meeting. The Shanghai City Pig, Beef, and Mutton Industry Association held a general meeting at Zhizhong Li in the French Concession on the afternoon of the 8th of this month. Representatives from urban and rural areas, Shanghai South, Zhabei, as well as Wusong, Jiangwan, Gaoqiao, Hongqiao, Longhua, Sanlintang, Caojing, Yangjing, Lan Nidu, Tangqiao, Yangjiadu, Lao B渡, Gaojiahang, Yangsiqiao, Pusongshi, Beixinjing, Xujiahui, Caojiadu, Zhenru, Lujiahang, Zhangjialou, Shiba Jian, Dai Nítang, Donggou, Zhangjiaqiao, Qichangzhan, Wang Mansiqiao, Hua Shao Gao Temple, Hongzhen, Qiujiangqiao, Fahua and other places, totaling more than 600 people, held a meeting as usual. Chairman Rong Qianchu reported that representatives were sent to Beijing to sincerely petition the Management Office and the Executive Yuan of the Central Government to abolish the slaughter tax and all miscellaneous taxes based on the principle of "one item, one tax" advocated by the late Premier, and to recognize the business tax. The circumstances of the discussions were reported. It was also discussed that the Municipal Finance Bureau took over the collection of the slaughter tax in the Chinese area of the city, using whole books of tickets, with the tax amount remaining the same, but all businesses were unwilling to buy. (1) It was resolved that armed police should be added to the slaughterhouses in Shanghai South and Zhabei today to supervise veterinarians exceeding their authority, and it was stated that if pigs were slaughtered without buying tickets, all white pigs would be detained and not allowed to be released. (2) It was resolved to adopt two methods: on the one hand, to submit a request to the Municipal Government to abolish the slaughter tax and all miscellaneous taxes and recognize the business tax; on the other hand, to petition the Executive Yuan of the Central Government again to implement the principle of "one item, one tax." Then, the pig, beef, and mutton industries jointly held a meeting and firmly agreed to the city-wide business tax and were willing to abolish the slaughter tax, as well as the inspection fees before and after slaughter, and the rural doctors' fees, and proceed in unison. The meeting adjourned at 5 p.m.

Finance Bureau's Statement. The person in charge of the Municipal Finance Bureau stated as follows yesterday: (1) The slaughter tax in the urban area has been approved by the central government and designated as a special fund for Jiangsu Province's education expenses. It has been levied for a long time. In April of this year, the Jiangsu Education Funding Management Office and the Shanghai Municipal Government agreed to hand it over to the Municipal Government for collection and disbursement. The Bureau was ordered to handle it, which was originally a collection on behalf of the Bureau and not a newly added tax. (2) This slaughter tax was contracted by merchants in 1919. At the end of April, the Bureau was ordered to directly collect it from May 1. At that time, representatives of the Su, Hu, and Ning gangs and other business people submitted petitions to contract the tax. The Bureau believed that direct collection was the principle of streamlining taxes and that merchants contracting the tax would inevitably lead to private gain and monopoly, which would be detrimental to both the government and the people. Therefore, after being ordered to take over, the Bureau immediately planned to proceed and rejected all requests for contracting. (3) After the Bureau took over, it continued to collect taxes according to the original tax rate when it was run by merchants, which was 3.9 cents per pig and 2 cents per sheep. The various meat businesses did not increase their burden. However, since the announcement of the collection, the various meat businesses have been waiting and seeing and have not come to purchase tax tickets. The Bureau initially believed that it was the beginning of the takeover and the time was very tight, and the meat business people may not have fully understood. It ordered the various collection offices to send personnel to persuade them separately, and temporarily registered the number of pigs slaughtered daily. Unexpectedly, until yesterday, the various meat businesses still used the excuse of waiting for the Association to resolve the issue and refused to purchase tax tickets. Now, in order to implement the laws and regulations, it is not convenient to delay any further, and it will be strictly enforced this morning. (4) When the slaughter tax in the urban area was previously handled by contractors, the various meat businesses had no objections. Even this time, when it was transferred to the Municipal Government for collection on behalf of the Municipal Government, representatives were recommended and submitted petitions to contract the tax. This shows that the various meat businesses have a proper understanding of the slaughter tax. Moreover, this tax revenue is allocated to Jiangsu Province's education expenses. It is hoped that meat business people will continue to pay it so that education expenses will not be affected.

Health Bureau's Advice. The Shanghai City Slaughter Tax was previously contracted by the county government to merchants on behalf of the Jiangsu Provincial Government. Now, because the Shanghai Municipal Government legally exercises its governance rights, it has been changed to be collected on behalf of the Municipal Finance Bureau, abolishing the contractor system, verifying the fees according to the number of animals, and eliminating private gain, so as to ensure that public funds are used for public purposes. The amount of tax collected is still the same as before, with a slaughter tax of 3.9 cents per head, with no increase. When the business tax is implemented in the future, the name of the slaughter tax will be changed. Unexpectedly, a small number of contractors, because they cannot contract the tax and cannot profit from it, have created various rumors and misled the meat merchants, leading them to stop importing goods. The Municipal Health Bureau, because it has been handling the inspection of livestock for many years and knows the inside information of the meat merchants very well, specially sent personnel to persuade the meat merchants not to be misled by the contractors and become sacrifices for the contractors' private gain. Most of the meat merchants have understood the background and are operating as usual.

Li Zongkan Escapes from Kidnappers' Den 99

Li Escapes from the Car

A Long Stand Off With Kidnappers

Even the Collar Was Torn

The Danger Was Imminent

Li Zongkan, the third nephew of Li Shizeng, a member of the Central Supervisory Committee, was about to be kidnapped by bandits at the entrance of his residence at 584 Lao Shenfu Road in the French Concession around 9 a.m. yesterday. Fortunately, Li was alert and escaped. The details are as follows:

Family Situation. Li Zongkan, courtesy name Shuta, is from Hebei Province, 31 years old, and is the nephew of Li Yuying, a member of the Central Supervisory Committee of the National Government. He studied in Paris and is the son-in-law of Zhou Jinjue, a famous postage stamp king from Anhui. Li obtained an engineering degree at a young age and returned to China two years ago. He was hired by the Dafang Construction Company at 112 Sichuan Road as an engineer and resided at 584 Lao Shenfu Road along the road in the French Concession. In addition to Li and his wife and a two-week-old boy, there were only three servants and a new chauffeur from Tongzhou, Liang Xiaodi, hired a month ago.

Daily Life. Because of his busy work, Li purchased a sedan car two years ago for transportation, with the concession number 2710. Li gets up at 8 a.m. every day, eats a little, and then goes to work around 9 a.m. He returns to his residence for lunch at noon, returns to the company at 2 p.m., and returns at 6 p.m. This is his usual routine. Only on holidays does he have time to go to his uncle's residence at 393 Fukaissen Road or his father-in-law's house at 141 Seymour Road.

Kidnappers Suddenly Arrive. Yesterday morning, Li got up at 8 a.m., washed and ate, and it was already 9:10 a.m. The chauffeur Liang Xiaodi had already prepared the car to wait. After a while, Li calmly went out and stepped into the car. Just as the chauffeur was about to start the engine, six kidnappers suddenly rushed out from the side of the road. Three bandits were in front and three bandits were in the back. One of the three bandits in front, wearing a dark silk robe, put a pistol against the chauffeur's waist, forbidding him to speak, and forced him to get out of the car. At that time, Li saw the situation and knew that he had encountered bandits, so he pretended to be calm, held the car door copper ring tightly with one hand, pushed it outward forcefully, and jumped out.

Extreme Danger. After Li jumped out of the car, he ran to the alley next door and fled into a French residence at 596 at the end of the alley. Unexpectedly, the bandits in the back dared to chase in with guns, chasing all the way to the courtyard. At that time, the owner of the house was out, the gate was tightly closed, and only a few servants were guarding the house. At that time, Li had nowhere to hide and was caught by the bandits. The two sides struggled for a long time. Li shouted for help. When the neighbors heard the alarm and gathered together, the two bandits released him and fled without a trace. As a result, Li's neck and collar were torn by the bandits. Fortunately, the bandits did not have time to shoot, so he was not seriously injured, but the shock was enough to scare him.

Two Suspects. At the same time, Li's family urgently called the French Police Station. After a while, the detectives arrived and chased in all directions. They chased to the vicinity of the Lujiawan Tram Company and intercepted two suspects with the same clothing as the bandits. They were taken to the police station for questioning. One side was escorted by several detectives and took Li to the residence of Central Committee Member Li Shizeng on Fukaissen Road. The detectives accompanied Li for lunch at Li's residence. At about 3 p.m., they accompanied him to the North Station, and Li took the 3:15 p.m. express train to Beijing for recuperation.

Huang Xianzhong Admits to Receiving Over One Million 100

Checks Were All Signed on Behalf of His Father

Chen Zhiquan and His Son Released on Bail

Chen Zhiquan, the president of the Shanghai Riyue Bank, and Chen Yuqing, the accounting clerk, were involved in embezzlement. The French court previously interrogated Chen and others, who claimed that Huang Chu Jiu's son, Huang Xianzhong, came to the bank on the day of Huang Chu Jiu's death and transferred over 1.1 million yuan. The checks and documents were also signed by Xianzhong on behalf of his father. They were ordered to summon Huang Xianzhong to court for questioning and verification. Yesterday, they were questioned again. On the creditor side, lawyers Yan Luqing and Xu Yannian attended the court for observation. First, the witness Huang Xianzhong was summoned to the court. After Judge Zhu compared the handwriting on the Riyue Bank's payment documents, they matched. Questioning Huang Xianzhong, he confessed that the Riyue Bank's checks and documents were actually signed by a civilian on behalf of his father. He signed them because after his father's death, someone came and ordered him to complete the unfinished procedures of his father's lifetime. The official said to Huang Xianzhong, "We did not summon you to court for questioning in the beginning. Before, we only relied on the one-sided words of the president Chen Zhiquan, which was not credible. Now that we have summoned you to court for questioning, you should bear criminal responsibility and pay a bail of 1.1 million yuan." At this time, Huang's representative, lawyer Tan Yigong, said that Huang Xianzhong had completely handed over his father's property to the accountant and was about to put it up for auction. He is now in a state of being unable to produce property. How can he find such a huge bail? He requested that the court allow him to be released on ordinary bail and summoned at any time. Accountant Pan Zhaobang claimed that he had found that the Riyue Bank had another expenditure of 805,000 yuan, which was handled by Chen Zaifeng and Wang Ziyuan of the Wanchun Silver Group. He requested that they be summoned to court for questioning. Lawyer Yao Zhaodi, the representative of President Chen Zhiquan and his son, said that his clients, Chen Zhiquan and his son, had been detained for a long time. It has been proven that the checks and documents were signed by Huang Xianzhong, and someone is responsible. He requested that Chen and his son be released. Judge Zhu said that Chen Zhiquan, Chen Yuqing, and Huang Xianzhong should each pay bail for release and must be summoned at any time. If they avoid being summoned, the bail will be confiscated. An arrest warrant was issued, and the case was adjourned for seven days, allowing witnesses to be summoned for questioning.

Authorities Protect. The Wusong fishing season is a major business of the year, and the market is very lively. Thieves Steal from the Aquatic Products School 102

Wusong Aquatic Products School Has Been Stolen from Three Times in a Row

They Tried to Steal Again Last Morning and Were Arrested by the Police

The Wusong Paotaiwan Aquatic Products School has had thefts on the 3rd of last month and the 1st of this month. The cases were reported to the Seventh District Public Security Bureau for investigation, but they have not been solved. Yesterday (the 9th) at about 1 a.m., the students of the school were all sound asleep. Suddenly, a thief broke a hole in the bamboo fence outside the school, entered, and broke the glass on the windows of the student dormitories, hoping to steal. Fortunately, he was discovered by a watchman, who immediately shouted "Catch the thief!" All the students in the school were awakened by the sound and sounded the alarm. At that time, Chang Jiaxin, the patrol captain of the Seventh District Public Security Bureau, was patrolling nearby with three policemen. Hearing the news, they rushed to the school to arrest the thief. When they arrived, the thief was gone. After the police surveyed the area, they knew that the thief was still hiding in the dark. However, the school grounds were vast, with many ditches and reeds, and it was late at night, making it difficult to find him. Patrol Captain Chang ordered two policemen to secretly monitor outside the school, while he took another policeman to patrol around. He also instructed the students in the school to be extra careful. At about 3 a.m., the thief thought that no one was guarding him, so he crawled out of the broken fence, hoping to escape. He was unexpectedly stopped and captured by the police. They found a wallet, three pawn tickets, three seals, a diary, three photos, two bunches of keys, and 64 yuan in cash on him. He was immediately escorted to the Seventh District. After Zhao Zezhou, the district chief, interrogated him, he confessed that his name was Wang Zhanqian, 26 years old, from Yuncheng, Shandong. He had previously been sentenced to seven months in prison by the court for theft and had just been released from prison at the beginning of last month. Because he had no food or shelter, he went to the school to steal. Including this time, it was his third time. The first time, he stole a large number of clothes, which he pawned at the Garbage Bridge. Other sundries were sold. The second time, he stole a typewriter, which he pawned for 33 yuan on Changbang Road in the French Concession, and a clock, which he sold for 80 cents. The remaining seals and other items were kept on his person. When asked how many people were involved in the theft, he confessed that he was the only one. The stolen goods were taken out of the school and placed in an empty thatched house on Paotaiwan, and transported to Shanghai in two batches. Today was the third time, but he was caught before he could start. All the black wool coat, yellow pants, and gray jacket he was wearing were stolen the first time. After verifying the confession, District Chief Zhao immediately prepared a document at 9 a.m. yesterday and sent the police to escort him to the Public Security Bureau for handling.

Wang Menglan Sues for Divorce, Sobbing in Court 103

Judge Sincerely Tries to Reconcile Them

Menglan Remains Unwilling

Feng Yeru was, in the past, married to Wang Menglan by her parents' arrangement. Wang, because she was illiterate, specifically provided funds for her education. The couple lived together for over ten years, enjoying harmonious marital life. Recently, disagreements arose, and their relationship deteriorated. Feng believed it was difficult to stay married until old age, so she left the Wang family, resided at the Young Women's Christian Association, and hired a lawyer to sue Wang in the Special District Local Court for abuse, claiming it was unbearable to live together, and requested permission to divorce Wang Menglan. However, since being sued, Wang also defended himself to the court, opposing the divorce and demanding that Feng Yeru return to live with him. Each held their own views, and the court had held several hearings. The judge hoped that both parties would set aside minor grievances and reconcile. Therefore, he did not rush to a judgment and instructed them to try to reconcile outside of court. However, Feng's unwillingness to rekindle their former affection was exceptionally firm, making reconciliation impossible. Yesterday morning, Judge Xu Wenrong continued the hearing. He first questioned Wang Menglan about the reconciliation situation. Wang stated that his only goal was for the plaintiff to continue living with him, with no other intention, but he was disappointed that he could not gain her understanding. Judge Xu then questioned Feng, who said that she really could not bear the abuse and vowed never to live with him again, not only unwilling to be a member of the Wang family in life but also unwilling to be a Wang family ghost in death. As she spoke, she seemed extremely heartbroken, tears streaming down her face, and then began to sob quietly, unable to speak. The judge immediately spoke to her gently, saying that Wang Menglan had not treated her poorly, making her study because she was illiterate, and she should not forget their past love over minor grievances. She should especially not lightly mention divorce due to unfavorable circumstances, especially since she still lacked the ability to support herself and would have difficulty maintaining her life living alone outside. The judge offered this advice in good faith, saying that marital harmony, where the defendant treated her well in the future, would be better than separation and living apart. However, she did not understand this reasoning, shaking her head repeatedly. Her younger brother, Feng Mengqi, was also in the courtroom listening. The judge then ordered him to persuade her gently. The siblings spoke for a long time, but to no avail. Therefore, after arguments between the two parties' lawyers, the judge ordered them to leave and await a scheduled judgment. The outcome depends on these final five minutes.

Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities Establishes a Shanghai West Advertising Management Office 104

Personnel Will Be Sent to Work on Wednesdays and Saturdays

The Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities manages advertisements within the city. It has already established advertising management offices in Shanghai South, Shanghai North, and Pudong. However, there was no office in the Shanghai West area. All advertising merchants had to handle matters at the Shanghai South Advertising Management Office, which was inconvenient. It is now known that the bureau has decided to temporarily establish the Shanghai West Advertising Management Office within the Sixth District General Office of the Caojiadu Public Security Bureau starting on May 16th. Afterwards, personnel will be sent by the bureau to work every Wednesday and Saturday. Those who post advertisements in this area can register and pay taxes at the management office nearby. A notice has already been posted.

Prohibition of the Sale of Sleeping Pills 106

Violators Will Be Heavily Fined and Their Pharmacies Closed

The sleeping pills sold in various pharmacies in the city mostly contain highly narcotic ingredients that can cause death. As a result, many frustrated young people use these drugs to commit suicide. If they are not strictly prohibited, the harm to society will be significant. The Shanghai Municipal Government yesterday received a notice from the Ministry of the Interior, stating that it approved the Ministry of Health's request to ban pharmacies from selling sleeping pills, which is in full compliance with Articles 6, 7, 14, and 15 of the Regulations on the Management of Pharmacists. A strict ban should be enforced to protect the people's peace and tranquility. Violators will be heavily fined, and the pharmacy may be closed as a punishment. After receiving the notice, the Municipal Government immediately forwarded it to the Social Affairs Bureau for strict compliance.

Guilds Request a Delay in Enforcement

Various tobacco retailers and sauce, wine, and grocery stores in the Chinese area of the city have failed to affix revenue stamps on their tobacco and alcohol licenses and have been investigated and fined by the bureau. The Tobacco Retailers' Guild, led by Chairman Chen Liangyu and the directors of the North and South offices, Qian Wenda and Wang Chengdong, went to the Revenue Stamp Bureau yesterday to personally explain the circumstances of the inadvertent omission and requested preferential treatment. They were granted permission for further review. The guild has already sent a special letter to the Municipal Public Security Bureau and various district offices, stating: "Regarding the recent inspection of revenue stamps by the Revenue Stamp Bureau, the majority of our members mistakenly believed that the tobacco and alcohol licenses were issued by the tax authorities and had official stamps, so they failed to affix revenue stamps. This is a common occurrence. According to the tax regulations, penalties should be imposed. However, these are small businesses with meager profits, and the heavy fines will cause unbearable hardship. Our guild has sent a letter to the Revenue Stamp Bureau requesting preferential treatment and lenient handling, which has been acknowledged and is under further review. We respectfully request that your bureau consider the merchants' difficulties and instruct the various district offices under your jurisdiction to temporarily suspend enforcement. We hereby send this letter for your attention."

Crossing the Road, Death Under the Wheels 111

Zhang Baohong Was Truly Pitiable

At approximately 9:00 AM the day before yesterday, streetcar number 334, driven by Hu Yuqing, was traveling from east to west on Broadway Road. At that time, Zhang Baohong, a 16-year-old from Jiangbei, was in a hurry to cross the road from north to south. However, behind the streetcar, car number 10476, driven by Yuan Wensi, came speeding along and violently knocked Zhang to the ground, causing serious injuries. A Japanese man in the car helped Zhang into the car and sent him to Tongren Hospital. Medical treatment was ineffective, and he died soon after. The hospital reported to the Huishan Police Station, who sent detectives to investigate. The body was taken to the Fielun Road Morgue. Yesterday morning, the Special District Local Court was notified and appointed prosecutor Guo Wei to come to the morgue for an examination. Guo took his seat in the public position. Zhang Baochang, the deceased's brother, complained that his younger brother had only been in Shanghai for two weeks from his original home in Jiangbei. He was playing on Broadway Road that day and was hit and killed by a car. He requested compensation. Guo verified the complaint and ruled that the deceased Zhang Baohong had been hit and killed by car number 10476. The body was handed over to his brother Zhang Baochang to arrange for the coffin and burial.

Floral Technician Commits Suicide by Poisoning 112

Cheng Xingkang, a 32-year-old from Cixi, Ningbo, worked as a floral technician in the Western-style underwear workshop at 9 Hehe Lane, Xiafei Road, French Concession. He was paid by piece, earning an average of sixty to seventy yuan per month. However, Cheng had a large debt. Recently, he was urgently pressed by creditors, which led him to a short-sighted act. He ingested poison before going to bed the night before last. It was not until 7:00 AM yesterday that a fellow worker discovered him already dead. The workshop owner, Xu Chengqing, reported to the police station, who dispatched detectives to investigate. They immediately took the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Morgue. Xu sent a telegram to Ningbo to notify the deceased's wife to come to Shanghai to take care of matters. Yesterday morning, the criminal section of the French Police Station reported to Judge Zhu Cheng of the French Court, who confirmed that the deceased had indeed committed suicide by poisoning before his death. He took his seat in the public position, questioned Xu about the deceased's life, and then authorized the deceased's family to collect the body themselves. As the deceased's family could not come to Shanghai in time, Tongren Fuyuan Hall was instructed to collect the body on their behalf to ensure hygiene.

Woman Carries a Gun to Assist Robbers 113

Detected and Captured by Detectives

Recently, robbers have found it inconvenient to carry guns due to the strict inspections by police officers along the way. However, they are unwilling to abandon weapons and commit robberies empty-handed. As a result, they are recruiting female accomplices to carry guns, as women are less likely to be searched by detectives due to politeness. However, this trick cannot last long. Similar cases have been cracked one after another recently. The men, however, remain ignorant and persist in treating it as a golden rule. At dusk the day before yesterday, two robbers, Tian Changfa and Chen A'er, intended to rob near the Great World. They followed the example of those before them by handing two handguns and eight bullets to their accomplice, Dong Shenshi. As they were about to set off from a certain place, Chief Detective Bai Zhongqi of the Huishi Police Station learned of the plan. He, along with Western Detective Zhaxu, led detectives to wait in ambush in front of the Great World on Edward Road. After some time, Tian and the others arrived leisurely. Upon a tip-off from an informant, they were intercepted together. The guns and ammunition were found in the woman's pockets. They were taken back to the police station, and each was detained. They were sent to the Special District Local Court yesterday. Because the details of their crimes had not yet been determined, Judge Wu only asked a few questions and ordered them to be remanded in custody pending further investigation.

Infant Corpse in the Huangpu River 114

At 7:00 AM yesterday morning, Chinese Constable No. 85 of the Water Patrol recovered the body of an infant, two or three months old, from the Huangpu River near the mouth of the Suzhou Creek. It was a male, with only the body, and no head. Some say that ignorant people have a superstitious belief that repeated births of children who die young are caused by reincarnated debtors. If the child's head is cut off after death and the body is thrown into a field or water, the child will not dare to reincarnate again. The child's body is probably one of such cases. It was taken away by the Life Saving Bureau for burial.

Two Robberies Occurred Yesterday Morning 115

Committed by the Same Gang

Two People Have Been Arrested

At about 1:00 AM yesterday morning, a passerby near Huanlong Road in the French Concession was robbed by four robbers, losing over seventy silver dollars and a long gown. Not long after, another passerby was robbed on Beile Road, losing about thirty or forty dollars. Unexpectedly, the two cases were committed by the same gang. After the robbers had enough, they went east along Edward Road. Patrolman Liu Jinrong No. 92 of the French Police Station happened to see them and thought they were suspicious. He immediately followed them secretly and reported to two Chinese constables of the Public Concession Police to intercept and arrest two people. After strict interrogation at the police station, the two confessed to robbing people on Huanlong Road and Beile Road. The police chief ordered them to be detained and sent to the court for prosecution.

Old Baidu Fire 116

Runtai Rag Shop, No. 40, Old Baidu Street, Nanshi, was a double-wide shop. At about 2:00 AM yesterday morning, a fire suddenly broke out on the second floor of the shop. The fire was very fierce and quickly broke through the roof. Fire brigades from various districts drove to the scene and extinguished the fire. The fire was extinguished after about an hour. In this fire, in addition to the two-story building of Runtai being burned, it also spread to the one-story building of the neighboring Dai Baoxing Incense Shop, the two-story building of Qingyuan Wool Shop, the two-story building of Hexingchang Western Iron Shop, and the one-story building of Hetaixing Gunny Sack Shop on the right. When the fire was raging, Patrolman Wang Can of the First District Police Station arrived after hearing the news and took Runtai's owner Wang Xiaocai and shop assistant Kong Linzhang from Taian to the district for preliminary interrogation. Wang Xiaocai confessed that he was 52 years old and from Ningbo, and that the fire was caused by the shop assistant carelessly throwing a lit cigarette butt into a pile of rags, causing the disaster. As the case involved a fire and the cause of the fire was highly suspicious, he was instructed to prepare a document and submit it to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation. It is said that Qingyuan Wool Shop had fire insurance, and Runtai also had fire insurance of 5,000 taels with a certain company. The rags stored on the first floor were not completely destroyed, only soaked in water. The loss of items burned on the second floor was not large.

Various Labor Unions' Expectations for Yang Youren 117

The various labor unions in Shanghai have expressed their opinions on this year's International Labour Conference's labor representative, which are recorded below: Yang Youren, the labor representative to the 15th International Labour Conference, has already left for Europe. Our associations have worked hard for many years to promote the labor movement and have high hopes for the International Labour Conference, which aims to improve the conditions of workers in various countries. Since the opening of the conference more than a decade ago, the government has appointed ministers or special envoys stationed in the country to represent it at each session. They have merely gone through the motions without fulfilling the expectations of the labor community and diminishing China's international standing. It is truly disheartening. In addition to the employer representative, the central government has appointed Yang as the labor representative for this year's conference. This is the first time that China's labor representative has attended the conference. This fulfills the requirements of the League of Nations charter, and the appointment is more prudent than making an unauthorized one. Furthermore, the mission of this year's conference is particularly important, including reporting on the implementation and ratification of conventions and electing the council, in addition to focusing on improving labor conditions. Moreover, as China is currently making efforts to negotiate legal rights, the Chinese representative has a major responsibility to stop foreign factories in China from failing to comply with Chinese labor laws. Therefore, the significance of this year's conference for improving China's international standing, advancing the Chinese revolution, and improving the welfare of Chinese workers is profound and unprecedented. With such a heavy responsibility, a labor representative must have experience in the labor movement, excellent knowledge, a sensitive mind, be fluent in foreign languages, have a history with the party and the nation, and be trusted by workers throughout the country. Otherwise, they will not be qualified to serve as a labor representative and will not be able to fulfill the mission of a labor representative. Moreover, the labor representative's first attendance at the conference makes them a model Chinese worker in the eyes of foreigners. Therefore, the importance of the appointment cannot be overstated by our associations. This time, the newspapers suddenly announced that Yang had been appointed by the central government as a representative. Whether his qualifications are suitable is still a question. However, Yang did not refuse the hardship and ignored everything. He resolutely went abroad to Europe under the central government's appointment to participate in the World Labour Conference of 55 countries. His motives are unknown, but his courage is commendable. We believe that he will follow the instructions of the central government, live up to the central government's appointment, and not repeat the mistakes of previous representatives and shame China internationally. Our associations' expectations of Yang are no different from those of the central government, so we will not repeat them. We offer our humble opinions as encouragement to Yang and hope that our fellow compatriots will take note. Silk Cocoon General Association Petitions the Jiangsu Provincial Government to Protect Cocoon Merchants 120

Huang Jinming, chairman of the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui Silk Cocoon General Association, submitted a document to Jiangsu Provincial Government Chairman Ye yesterday regarding the protection of the cocoon market, stating, "Regarding the protection of cocoons, advance preparations should be made in accordance with the regulations and methods of past years. We respectfully request your review and instructions to the military, political, and civil officials of each cocoon region to strictly protect the market in order to ensure the safety of farmers and merchants. It has been found that the cocoon market in Jiangsu typically opens after the Little Fullness solar term. Each year, the General Association drafts protection measures and submits them to the National Government, which distributes them to various provinces and regions for implementation, and prints them into protection guidelines, which are submitted to your office for forwarding to the military, political, and civil agencies in each jurisdiction for reference and implementation. This has allowed for thorough protection and has been deeply appreciated. The cocoon market is approaching this year, and the social situation is relatively stable. However, there is a sense of caution in areas with multiple waterways far from the county seat. Most of the cocoon-producing areas in Jiangsu Province rely on waterway transportation. At that time, the flow of silver and goods requires reliable troops to provide protection at all times to prevent accidents. It is the duty of the General Association to list all the items that need to be protected, such as the transportation of cash and the delivery of cocoon packages, with dates, based on past practices. We respectfully request your office to preside over the matter and order the cocoon-producing areas to instruct the troops stationed there and the Public Security Bureaus of the various prefectures to protect the market in accordance with the regulations. In addition to submitting this to the National Government and printing 100 copies of the regulations for your office to forward to the various cocoon-producing counties and military and police officials in charge of protection for reference and implementation, the reasons for the advance request for protection of the cocoon market are hereby attached for your consideration and implementation. We also request your instructions for compliance."

Inland River Steamer Operation Permits 121

Response from the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Construction

Notice from the Trade Association

Following the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Construction's implementation of issuing inland river steamer operation permits, the local Inland River Steamer Trade Association, due to difficulties in complying with the ten application procedures, listed four items and telegraphed for amendments or flexibility: (1) The route filled in on the Ministry of Transportation's permit is comparatively longer. Now, the application form for the operation permit requires filling in the actual route traveled, which may not match the Ministry's permit. Flexibility is requested. (2) Request to waive the submission of a business license copy. (3) For leased steamers, the shipowner's name on the Ministry's permit will inevitably differ from the Shipping Bureau's name. Flexibility is also requested. (4) Request to waive the need for a temporary operation permit. Now, the response from the Department of Construction provides instructions for each item as follows: (1) The fifth section of the application form for the operation permit should state the starting and ending points of the current route and the locations passed, consistent with the details listed on the Ministry's permit. However, the locations passed on the application form must be filled in based on the actual locations navigated. If there are mid-way branch lines and the route is a detour, the locations within the branch lines should be added to the list of locations passed. (2) If there is currently no business license, it is permitted to submit it after obtaining the operation permit. (3) According to the Ministry's regulations, once a steamer is leased, the original license should be cancelled, and the lessee should fill in "leased" and apply for a new license. There is no reason for the Shipping Bureau's name to differ on the Ministry's permit due to the leased ship. The requested flexibility cannot be granted. (4) If an emergency or disaster occurs, assistance from other steamers will not be restricted, but only for rescue purposes. If, at the starting or ending point, another steamer is used as a replacement under the pretext of the original steamer's machinery damage, it will be considered a replacement service, and operation is not allowed without a temporary operation permit. After receiving the response, the association immediately printed the four instructions and notified all affiliated shipping bureaus, requesting them to comply with the ten procedures for applying for an operation permit previously issued by the Department of Construction, and to complete the various forms according to regulations, referencing the four instructions, and submit them to the local county construction bureau to apply for the operation permit, in compliance with the law.

Silk Factory Workers Demand Restoration of Old Wages 122

Social Bureau Schedules Mediation for the 12th

39,000 female workers, 3,600 male workers, and 18,000 child laborers in silk factories in the fourth and sixth districts of the city have been subject to a temporary wage reduction last year, which is rare in all industries. Initially, it was based on labor-management mutual assistance and understanding, upholding the spirit of cooperation to develop the industry, and reluctantly sacrificing by calculating wages at 85%. Since the reduction, gold prices have soared, and commodity prices have risen accordingly, making life increasingly difficult for workers. Therefore, the wages earned through hard work and sweat cannot provide for the family, and they cannot even eat their fill, inevitably leading to death. They have no choice but to request that the employers restore the original wages from May 1st. The labor union has sent a letter to the trade association, and the trade association has already held a meeting a few days ago and resolved to issue 57 cents according to the Wuxi method, raising the wages for four workers to three. The union was first notified that the current situation will remain unchanged for the month, and a date will be set for implementation from June 1st. In order to resolve the issue quickly, the Municipal Social Bureau has scheduled a meeting with the Silk Factory Trade Association and the Silk Reeling Unions of the fourth and sixth districts on the morning of the 12th at 9 a.m. to conduct mediation.

Drunkard Attempts Suicide by Stabbing and Drowning 125

Fortunately Rescued by Villagers

Cao Zhende, a carpenter from Fenghua, 43 years old, residing at No. 9 Rongqing Lane, Tiantong'an Road, is addicted to alcohol and only happy when drunk. He often buys drinks from Yongmaokang Hotel on Yongxing Road, spending about 20 cents each day. However, due to his lack of funds, he has accumulated over 100 cents in debt for the past nine days. The hotel owner has repeatedly demanded payment, but Cao was unable to repay and could only sigh. Last night, he suddenly went insane and stabbed his throat with scissors behind people's backs. Although injured, he did not die and ran out of the house to commit suicide by drowning in the river. Fortunately, he was spotted and rescued by villagers, who handed him over to the police to be sent to the hospital for treatment, and his life was saved.

Native Cloth Traders Request Tax Exemption 128

Request Wang Yansong to Propose to the National Assembly

The Native Cloth Traders Association sent a letter to Wang Yansong, the city's representative to the National Assembly, yesterday, stating: "We are writing to you concerning the export of hand-woven native cloth by our industry. Due to customs disputes over tariffs, our association previously sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to forward to the Unified Tax Bureau, providing evidence of tax-exempt history and examining the Bandit Suppression Unified Tax Regulations, which stipulate 'one tax per item.' We detailed the reasons why we should be exempted from taxation and petitioned the Ministry of Finance and the Customs Administration. On April 16th, our association, together with the Shanghai Yarn and Cloth Traders Association, sent representatives to meet with Director Xie of the Unified Tax Bureau. We were informed that the Bureau had consulted with the Customs Administration to instruct the General Customs Office to order the Customs to exempt exports. More than 20 days have passed, and the native cloth traders have suffered significant losses due to prolonged suspension of transportation. Furthermore, goods cannot be unloaded, and goods sent are held at customs declaration agents. Various considerations make us deeply concerned about the dangers of fire and water. Therefore, we are writing again to request the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to request the Ministry of Finance and the Customs Administration to quickly resolve the issue. Our association also sent a telegram on the 28th, but we have not yet seen the approval order arrive in Shanghai, and the Customs has not yet announced it. Merchants are as if they are in a five-mile fog, and the losses to our industry are unprecedented in a century. The members of our association are in positions of responsibility and must accept this, but we also request that the National Government uphold its emphasis on people's livelihood, the resolution to promote domestic goods, and the 'one tax per item' system. We request that you maintain your credibility. We are enclosing a copy of Yu's telegram, requesting your representation to ask the Ministry of Finance and the Customs Administration to order the Customs to announce the order immediately, to uphold the late Premier's attention to people's livelihood, and to comfort the hundreds of thousands of merchants who are longing for rain in a drought. Furthermore, today's newspaper reports the announcement of the public export tariff regulations, with 270 items divided into six categories. Native cloth is in the category exempted from customs duties. At this critical juncture, we urge you to strive to achieve our goal and restore our industry's livelihood. We would be extremely grateful."

Robbery on Tongfu Road Yesterday Morning 129

At around 6:30 a.m. yesterday, eight robbers came to No. 90 Tongfu Road in the Public Concession. Two of them took out handguns and guarded the front and back doors. The remaining robbers entered the rooms upstairs and intimidated the owner's maids, arbitrarily searching and looting. They escaped after half an hour. Donates Sewing Machines to the Orphanage

The Zhabei Orphanage of the Chinese Child Welfare Association focuses on scientific methods in its facilities and emphasizes life experience in its education. The purpose of the orphanage is to provide orphans with comfortable families and childless families with children to care for. The orphanage has a school and also teaches crafts, with a focus on sewing, as it is beneficial for practical use in the home. However, the orphanage has limited funds and relies entirely on the assistance of enthusiastic child welfare advocates in society. The Singer Sewing Machine Company, knowing that the orphanage is well-run, generously donated a fine sewing machine. From now on, the children of the orphanage will not only be able to practice in person, but also easily make clothes. The company can be said to be enthusiastic about child welfare, generous, and benevolent.

Ivory and Bone Craft Industry Requests Reduction of Business Tax 138

The Shanghai Ivory and Bone Craft Industry Association, due to the business tax, previously drafted a proposal by the Finance Bureau, stipulating that the ivory and bone craft industry should be taxed at 10 per mille. The association has held several meetings to discuss this and, based on the facts, does not recognize it as a sales industry but only as a manual manufacturing industry. It should be taxed at 20 per mille of the capital, according to regulations, and does not want to be heavily taxed. It is reported that it has submitted the situation to the municipal authorities and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, etc., requesting approval and revised regulations to relieve business difficulties.

Education News and Discussion

On Children's Literature Revisited 142

(In Response to Mr. Wu Yanyin) Shang Zhongyi (I)

During the annual meeting of the Chinese Children's Education Society in Shanghai, Zhongyi proposed a discussion of children's literature. Due to limited time, it was not possible to express all that I wanted to say. I am now writing specifically about "fairy tales" (including stories of gods and immortals and other fantasy stories) to share my thoughts and seek correction from colleagues.

When children are developing and learning to understand the real environment and observe natural phenomena, adults responsible for guiding them should not, unless there is a sufficient reason, give them a concept that conflicts with natural phenomena. There are no such things as gods and monsters in the world, and birds and animals cannot speak human languages. Therefore, unless there is sufficient reason, children's literature should not contain materials that contradict natural laws and principles. "Whether there is sufficient reason" is the key to the whole situation, which is the standard for choosing fairy tales. Let's try to carefully evaluate the value of fairy tales and see if there is a reason to maintain their position in children's literature. If there is a reason, let's see if it is sufficient.

"Evaluation of the Value of Fairy Tales"

(1) Inspiring Imagination: Because fairy tales have been circulating for a long time, most people follow the old path and never talk about their value. Even if they occasionally discuss it, they are blocked by the words "inspiring imagination." Therefore, to this day, fairy tales can still maintain their important position in children's literature, occupying most of children's reading time. We cannot prove that "inspiring imagination" is definitely not possible, but we are afraid it is difficult to determine that it is possible. Between possible or impossible, we still have three doubts:

(1) Is the organized, creative imagination in science and art (Creative Imagination) the same as bizarre, whimsical reverie (Reverie)? (2) If they are not the same, which type is likely to be elicited by stories of gods and fairies? (3) If they are the same, if fantasy is the creative imagination that produces, why is the legendary skill of Changsang from two thousand years ago not realized in China but realized in Germany with X-rays?

Under these circumstances, although we cannot say that fairy tales absolutely cannot inspire imagination, we are convinced that the ability of science stories and natural reading materials to inspire imagination is definitely no less than that of fairy tales. The heaven-defying and earth-shrinking magic methods in science stories, even if Nezha were to appear and Andersen's puppets were born, would have to concede defeat. The various amazing methods of adapting to the environment in the biological world of natural reading materials would probably make Sun Wukong, who can only perform seventy-two transformations, smile wryly.

Important News

Fourth World Education Conference to be Held in July 143

Welcoming Chinese Educators to Attend

The World Education Association is a collection of international educational groups, with the aim of enhancing international friendship, promoting international culture, and seeking the progress of education in various countries. The inaugural conference was held in San Francisco in 1923, followed by the first conference in Edinburgh, Scotland, in 1925, the second conference in Canada in 1927, and the third conference in Switzerland in 1929. China has sent representatives to all of them. Dr. Guo Bingwen was elected as the vice president of the association for three consecutive terms. At the third conference, he and Dr. Zhang Boling were elected as directors for the Chinese side. The fourth conference will be held this year, scheduled from July 27 to August 2 in Denver, Colorado, USA. The scenery there is beautiful and it is one of the educational centers of the United States. Educators from China are welcome to attend, whether as a group or individually. Dr. Liu Zhanen, president of Shanghai College, attended the third conference and is very familiar with the situation. Domestic educators who are interested in participating can directly write to Mr. Liu for detailed inquiries.

Academic Circles Commemorate May 9th 144

Labor University: The Labor University held a May 9th National Humiliation Commemoration at the school in Jiangwan yesterday morning at 8:00 a.m. President Zhang Yuanruo of the College of Social Sciences presided over the ceremony. First, Zheng Xigu spoke about the events of the Twenty-One Demands and the efforts that should be made in the future. Then, Professor Kang Xuanyi interpreted the difference between national humiliation and personal shame.

Shanghai College: Shanghai College held a May 9th National Humiliation Commemoration yesterday morning at 11:30 a.m. President Liu delivered a speech, stating that it is extremely appropriate for us to not forget the national humiliation and hold commemorations every year. However, the method of avenging the humiliation lies in the efforts of the masses, active construction, and national strength to resist foreign aggression. The border issue is particularly important. Therefore, the school advocates research to arouse the people's inspiration for border affairs and to consolidate our border. He specially invited Mr. Chen Jichang of the Kangzang Infantry Corps to give a lecture at the school. Mr. Chen spoke about the mild climate, beautiful mountains and rivers of Kangzang, no less than the Central Plains, and its rich mineral resources, abundant everywhere. It is vast in area and sparsely populated, urgently needing to be developed and filled to prevent strong neighbors from coveting it and to protect our inherent territory.

Shanghai Women's High School: Shanghai Women's High School held a May 9th National Humiliation Commemoration Conference yesterday morning at 9:00 a.m. Principal Wu Ziqian reported on the origins of the May 9th National Humiliation. Five Group Sports Meet 160

Mullins Wins Championship

—Dong Zhaobin Takes First Place in the Youth Division—

—The Youth Team is Composed of Baihong Team Members—Yesterday They Rested to Prepare for Today's Match Against Jiangnan—The Shanghai Five Giants, Youth, West, Aviation, Mullins, and American Public, held a joint sports meet at the American Public School sports field on Avenue Petain yesterday afternoon at 2:30 PM, which concluded at 6:00 PM. Mullins won the team championship with 54.5 points, and Dong Zhaobin of the Youth team won the individual championship with 16 points.

Reasons for the Youth Team's Failure

The Five Giants League has an international character, which has attracted countless enthusiastic Chinese and Western spectators. The Chinese spectators cheered for the Youth team. However, when the declaration of war was issued, only Dong Zhaobin and Zong Zean from the Youth team appeared in uniform, while the rest were missing. Spectators said that most of the Youth team members are from the Baihong team, and they will participate in today's match against Jiangnan. For the sake of cultivating strength, they put the important international competition behind them, which caused great displeasure and discussion. Ni Xiaoben, an official of the Youth team, forgot his personal interests and bravely volunteered to put on his uniform, showing the spirit of four years ago, and also won a point in the hurdles, adding some glory. The three members of the Youth team seemed to be fighting for survival among millions of soldiers, working hard and relentlessly, trying to defeat the majority with a few, and almost snatched the runner-up spot from the American Public team. Dong Zhaobin participated in four events, winning first place in two and second place in two, totaling 16 points, taking the lead in the individual overall standings. Zong Zean also scored three points. If the entire team had participated, the champion of the Five Giants would undoubtedly belong to the Youth team. It is a pity that because of today's game, the brave warriors and generals had the suspicion of avoiding the important and taking the easy, abandoning the former for the latter.

Free Talk

A Word or Two 161

— Qiu Shui

A husband obsessed with dancing and a wife obsessed with dancing should be like a dancing bear in a circus, bound with an iron chain.

Old-fashioned women are like old-fashioned wooden furniture. If you use them carefully, they can last a lifetime. But modern women are like the cars that are popular on the market, many are counterfeit and don't last long.

A woman can love any hair on her husband's head, but a hair found on his collar will raise some questions.

Whatever he can do, he does himself. Whatever he can't do, he teaches others.

Young people can forgive others but not themselves. Old people can forgive themselves anything, but will never forgive others.

Success in business cannot be conditional. What is conditional is compromise, not success.

A long period of happiness can cause great pain.

Those who do not believe in themselves cannot believe in others.

Rational people follow the environment, irrational people want the environment to follow them. Therefore, the progress of culture is mostly due to the efforts of irrational people.

Men are smarter than women, not because they have more experience than women, but because their ability to acquire experience is better than women's.

No intelligent person can reveal all their opinions. Straightforward people are often not intelligent.

A Record of Boxer Jiang Dafu 162

— Chen Boying

The mountains and rivers of Sichuan are magnificent and nurture talent. Thus, men of letters often lead the world. And martial arts are especially skilled in the world. My friend Zhu Qiufang, a native of Chengdu, said that there is a person named Jiang Dafu in his hometown, a famous boxer. I have seen his performance skills. He piled a hundred bricks on the ground and slapped them with his hand. If people asked him to break a certain number of bricks, he would break that number of bricks. Or if he was told to break a certain brick, he would break that brick without fail. If he wanted to break them all, he would press down once from top to bottom, and they would all be like powder. He also stood on the ground, with a rope tied to each of his left and right feet. Dozens of people pulled in different directions, but they could not move him even a bit. He also let people hit him with a stick, like hitting a broken quilt. If he was cut with a blade, his whole body would be like stone, and the blade would be completely curled. Dafu already had a great reputation. One day, a guest came to visit and asked to compare skills. When they met, they bowed to each other. The guest's bow was accompanied by a gust of wind, because the guest secretly injured him with five hundred pounds of force. Dafu knew his intention and also responded with five hundred pounds of force. The guest then knew that he could not be insulted. After sitting down, he used his power to break the chair. Dafu saw that the chair was broken and immediately got up and apologized, saying that the chair was not suitable for sitting on, and that he was guilty of slighting the guest. He then lifted the stone drum in front of the steps to replace it. The guest looked at the place where the stone drum was pinched by his hand, as if it had been chiseled. He looked back at Jiang's chair, which had been half-submerged in the ground but was intact. Then they went out together to the field. Beside the field was an ancient pagoda with seven stories, covered with withered vines. The wind chimes rang from time to time. The guest took off his clothes and looked around, saying, "I should first put this thing in place." He then hung his clothes on the fifth floor of the pagoda, fluttering like a swallow between the upper and lower floors. Dafu said, "Hanging it here is good, but I'm afraid that the strong wind will blow it down and stain it. Please let me change it for you." He then moved the clothes to the top of the pagoda. His movements were as fast as lightning, and there was no sound. The guest judged himself to be no match and repeatedly expressed his admiration. In the end, he did not compete and left. Dafu traveled back and forth in Sichuan and often rescued him from thieves. The thieves hated him very much and waited for him every day. One night, Dafu went out, and the thieves followed him. Dafu did not realize it at first. When the thieves caught up with him, they raised their iron rods and hit him hard, thinking that Dafu would be injured and fall. However, when the rod was about to fall, Dafu immediately raised two fingers to catch it and held the rod so that it could not move. Dafu then ran. The thieves' strike was indeed fierce, but since the rod could not fall, their bodies were suspended three feet off the ground. Dafu ran, and the thieves were very frightened and begged him repeatedly. Dafu said, "You rats dare to plot against me! If I were to throw you forward, you would be dead. Now, I will lend you your mouth to spread the word, and don't provoke my anger again." He then released them and left. Qiufang also said that Dafu's encounter with his teacher was especially strange. Dafu was poor as a child and not very intelligent by nature. He was a cowherd. When he led the cow and the cow refused to go, he would kneel down and bow to it. When asked what he meant, he would say, "When the mistress gets angry, the master always does this." Therefore, his companions often insulted him. One day, he drove the cow out and went a little further, entering a neighboring village. There was a small temple in the village, which was very dilapidated. When he was about to return home, the cow suddenly became stubborn and would not accept the whip. Dafu bowed firmly, but the cow still would not go. The temple door opened, and a monk came out and asked what was wrong. Dafu said, "The cow is very angry, and I am begging it." The monk said, "This is a cow, why do you need to do this?" He took the cow's rope with one hand, as if leading a dog. The cow dared not fall behind. When they were about to reach Dafu's home, the monk said goodbye. The next day, Dafu went to the same place again. The cow again refused to go. Just as he was at a loss, the monk came out again. Dafu pleaded with him. The monk said, "I am not a cowherd, how can I drive the cow for you every day? If you are here, you will meet me, but what about elsewhere?" Dafu thought for a long time and then said, "Then please teach me your skills, monk." The monk said, "Your nature is pure and simple, which is good. But you must persevere to achieve success." Thereupon, Dafu followed the monk to learn martial arts every day. After ten years of training, he became invincible in Sichuan. The monk's name was Foyin.

Interesting Prison Life 163

— Shi Yan Ye

A returning traveler from the north said that in the Third Prison of Tianjin, there are many political prisoners. Confined behind iron bars, they have nothing to do. Recently, with the permission of the prison guards, they agreed to play basketball. The value of a ball is several gold, which they cannot afford. So they begged for a cow's bladder, inflated it, and wrapped it layer upon layer with rubber paper to make it strong. Although its elasticity is not as good as a leather one, it is still quite satisfactory for throwing back and forth. The construction of basketball hoops would cost even more, so they couldn't prepare them. They came up with a whimsical idea and ordered two people to stand on chairs facing each other and join hands to form a ring, which also looked like a basket. Since the establishment of this basketball team, they have been happily throwing the ball around in the prison yard every day, saying that it is both a way to make the best of their suffering and to practice exercise. Those who see it can't help but laugh. The traveler also said that on New Year's Day this year, they even held a celebration party in prison. In addition to the usual speeches, there were also performances. Chinese martial arts, crosstalk, new dramas, and Peking opera were all available. All costumes and props were made of paper, or modified from ordinary clothes. In the "Empty City Stratagem" play, Marquis Wu made a Bagua robe out of a large shirt glued with paper, banana leaves for feather fans, and paper for a Lun scarf. He leaned leisurely against the city tower made from a modified bed sheet and sang loudly. His singing and acting were excellent, making him the most outstanding act of the entire variety show and earning him frequent applause. Other performances were also very watchable. The stage on that day was not built at first, but was made by drawing lines on the ground with white powder. The audience stood outside the lines. Some were relatives and friends of the prisoners, and some were acquaintances of the prison guards. Those without any connections were not allowed to enter. In addition to the variety show, there was also a wall newspaper, which mainly contained texts and pictures. The works were also quite good.

Train vs. Car Race 164

— Da Mei

The Special Express Train Could Not Beat the Car. The Car Arrived Half an Hour Early

Train racing was discovered in England a few years ago. The initiators were the train companies traveling between Scotland and England. They often divided their trains into groups to compete in order to increase the speed of the trains. However, in recent years, this trend has gradually declined and is rarely seen. On the European continent, however, there are races between trains and cars, which are more interesting and novel than train-versus-train races. However, this kind of competition often leads to danger, and pedestrians on the road are particularly inconvenienced. It is expected that this trend will soon be greatly reduced.

A few months ago, New Zealand had a major race between a car and a train. The race was from Wellington to Auckland. Before and after the race, the railway bureau reported it to the people of the whole country via radio. At one time, many people came from afar to watch. Although the competition time was in the evening and the places passed through were mostly rugged, the car actually arrived at the destination half an hour earlier than the train.

On Dreams 165

— Tao Zaidong

In this publication last month, Mr. Yu recounted the disaster of the Da Ji Wheel. A person named Mr. Yi, carrying $2,400 in cash, boarded a fishing boat owned by a Mr. Wang, and they agreed to split the money equally. Mr. Wang greedily seized all the money and pushed Mr. Yi into the water to drown him. That night, Mr. Yi's son dreamed that Mr. Yi told him about what happened. He immediately went to Hong Kong and waited for the Mr. Wang's fishing boat to enter the port. He reported the case to the authorities, who boarded the boat and found the stolen money. Mr. Wang was brought to justice. Scientists would laugh at this. But in my life, I have personally experienced and heard about dreams that are so strange and incredible, which are undoubtedly true. And consulting the records of thousands of years, are all those storytellers fools? After summarizing them broadly, two causes can be identified: one is caused by sincere feelings, and the other is caused by accumulated resentment. Sincere feelings, such as what is said in "Liaozhai," the soul of the affectionate woman arrives beside the pillow, and the good friend thousands of miles away still recognizes the road in the dream. Accumulated resentment, such as what happened to Mr. Yi. There is an extremely similar case to Mr. Yi's. During the turmoil of Erzhu Zhao in the Northern Wei Dynasty, Prince Chengyang, Wei, sought refuge with Kou Zuren, the magistrate of Luoyang. Because they had old friendship, Zuren said to his sons, "I heard that the reward for capturing Prince Wei is very high. The one who captures him will become a marquis with a thousand households. Wealth and honor have arrived today." Then he beheaded Wei and sent his head. When Wei first sought refuge with Zuren, he brought 100 catties of gold and 50 horses. Zuren was greedy for his wealth, so he did this. Zhao suddenly dreamed that Wei said, "I have 200 catties of gold and 100 horses at Zuren's house. You can take them." At dawn, Zhao surrounded Zuren. Wei took his gold and horses. Zuren secretly told people, hoping to be forgiven. He said that he had indeed obtained 100 catties of gold and 50 horses. Zhao suspected that he was hiding some. Based on Wei's dream, Zhao searched Zuren's rooms. There were 30 catties of gold and 30 horses, all of which were sent to Zhao. It still wasn't enough. Zhao was angry. He seized Zuren, hanged him from a tall tree, dropped a large stone on his feet, and whipped him to death. People at the time considered it retribution. This is described in detail in the "Records of the Buddhist Monasteries of Luoyang." Judging from Mr. Yi's case, can anyone still say that Su Dongpo's ghost stories are all nonsense?

Short News Recently, Mr. Chen Qiufeng, Mr. Huang Huaisheng, and others established the Xinguang Sound Film Company and started filming "After the Rain, the Sky Clears." They sent director Xia Chifeng, along with actors Lin Ruxin, Gu Baolian, and Huang Naishuang, to Japan to record the sound. The total length is 40,000 feet. After Xia Chifeng arrived at the port, he immediately started recording the sound after unpacking his luggage. The sound quality is clear, and the results are very good. It will be released in China soon. (Hongchu)

India Travelogue (48) 166

— Ling Hua

9th: Together with University Professor Venkateswaran K. G., I went to the headquarters of the Indian University. In the evening, the president of the university summoned the professors, about thirty or forty people, for a debate. Mr. Venkateswaran read my manuscript, and the participants raised many questions. I answered them, and they were all very happy. The chairman, Abdhruva, the president, signed his approval. Currently, there are many Marxist study groups in various parts of India, and many of their books are printed. Indians have no resistance to them, so there is no prohibition either. Marxist scholars asked me many questions. I explained that I am a scholar of human nature and society and do not oppose Marx. However, I explained that materialism is not yet sufficient.

10th: The faculty and staff of the Normal School and the Indian School, together with the principals of the two schools, held a joint debate session, with about forty people. I answered them one by one, and they were all very happy. The two principals are very enthusiastic about cultural reform. Naren Misha asked me to take a photo with him and invited me to jointly organize the Asian Education Association. When I return to Varanasi, I will convene a conference to discuss it. On this day, I met Dr. Shri Bhagavan Das, a prominent figure in the Varanasi political faction. He invited me to stay at his home, which has a garden, and introduced me to Gandhi, the leader of India. According to Bhagavan Das, world peace requires promoting matriarchy to abolish war and promoting motherly ways to teach unruly children so that masculinity can be reformed.

11th: I got up at 4:00 AM. Bhagavan Das, who is over sixty years old, also got up. He sent his son to accompany me to the train to Allahabad to visit Gandhi. Before dawn, Bhagavan sent me off very warmly. I boarded the train at 6:00 AM and arrived at 11:00 AM. I read poetry on the train. Seeing the wheat seedlings growing, I couldn't help but feel the song of Wei Zi about wheat growing. It said, "Wheat grows tall and lush, and the millet grows abundantly." I thought of the difficult land of India, where freedom is not easily obtained. It rained on this day. I first heard about the dry and wet seasons in India, thinking that there would be no rain in the dry season. But now I know that this is not the case. It still rains in the dry season, but only once every few weeks. In northern China, it often rains only once every few months in winter. Winter in northern India is roughly the same as in China. I have not yet reached its extreme north, but I already feel quite cold and am wearing a cotton robe. However, there is no frost, and the plants are always green. However, being close to the snowy mountains in the north, its coldness can be imagined.

Rotary Club Speaking Event

The Turning Point in the Hawthorne Case (9) 167

— Cheng Xiaoqing

(3) In the Police Station

So I told Zhang Baoquan the whole story. Finally, I added, "This matter is very clear. The thief was mixed among the Gao family's guests at the time. He used some method to steal the necklace and quietly slipped out. After taking a few steps, he realized your detective was following him. He became nervous and wanted to transfer the stolen goods in order to escape. Unfortunately, your detective fell for his trick and became entangled with me, allowing the thief to escape right under his nose." Zhang Baoquan exclaimed in surprise, "Oh, so that's how it was!" He then turned his head and scolded Qiu Kui, "You useless idiot! How could you do such a thing? You're supposed to be a detective. Even if you don't know Mr. Bao, you should have at least heard of his reputation. How could you still be so stubborn after Mr. Bao explained his name? You're a disgrace!" Qiu Kui lowered his head, not even daring to look up. His humble and fearful state was almost comical. He stammered, "I deserve to die. I misheard. Please forgive me this time, Mr. Bao." He suddenly turned around and repeatedly bowed to me. I felt a bit embarrassed. It's not uncommon for these ignorant people to be arrogant before and obsequious after. If I insisted on retaliating on the spot, it would seem that I lacked magnanimity. So, I mediated, saying, "Mr. Zhang, although his initial rudeness and humiliation towards me were inappropriate for a detective, since it was due to a misunderstanding, I can forgive him. However, this case is clearly very serious. Because he was being unreasonable at the time, he allowed the villain to escape. So, nothing else matters. How should the thief's whereabouts be investigated? Mr. Qiu should be responsible." Zhang Baoquan stamped his foot again and said to Qiu Kui, "Damn it, damn it! You clearly ruined this case. If you want to keep your job, you must take responsibility for tracking down that person." Qiu Kui bent his back like a bow and repeatedly replied, "I recognize this bad guy. I will definitely do it. I will definitely do it." After saying these words, he didn't dare say anything else and bowed deeply again before walking out of the office with his head lowered. I silently thought that arrogance and boastfulness when successful, and flattery and subservience when unsuccessful, are the usual tricks of petty people. It's truly laughable and pathetic.

Finance 168

Gold Price Rises Six Taels and a Half

The trend is upward. Yesterday, the 9th, the gold price rose again. The situation is peaceful, and the initial increase was only two taels. However, transactions were frequent, likely because the silver market suddenly reported a drop, stirring up people's emotions. The market opened with a sharp rise, and buyers were very enthusiastic, quickly pushing through the 740 tael mark. Later, due to increased selling and a slight easing of exchange rates, the listed price did not change, causing a downward trend, falling three or four taels. Nevertheless, industry sentiment was hesitant, with advances and retreats, ultimately settling at slightly above 38 taels. This morning, the general trend seems bearish. Because the market is closed on Saturdays, looking back from the beginning of the week to yesterday, the highest price reached 44 taels and 8 mace, and the lowest price was 31 taels. This six-day range was only 13 taels and 8 mace. Overall, the net increase was six taels and some change.

Sharp Rise at the Open. The June market opened this morning with a jump of more than seven taels, to 739 taels, because the "big bar" was down by 1/16th (due to an expected rise overnight). The silver price also dropped by 1/8th, as did private telegraphs, especially with continuous selling from the United States. Before long, Zhifengyong and others sold, reducing the price by two taels. However, Dadecheng, Yuanmaoyong, and others came to buy, and banks traded June English gold at 375, causing a surge of more than three taels, reaching 40 taels and 5 qian at 9:20 AM. In a flash, China Bank sold June-July English gold at 375 to 4375, and the Dalian Gang and Tianfengyong, Tongchang, etc., also sold, immediately suppressing it by more than two taels. When Xianling announced the price, it was 38 taels and 2 qian, with the posted price remaining the same, at 8 taels and 56 qian. Qianchangxiang, Yuanheng, and others sold. At 9:40 AM, it was 37 taels. Hengxing, Fuyu, and Yongfeng bought. At 10:00 AM, it was 8 taels and 8 qian. Afterward, there were fluctuations of two taels. After 10:30 AM, selling off positions was quite active, making it difficult for prices to hold steady, and they weakened again, falling to 36 taels and a half around 10:50 AM. Before long, Hengxing, Yongfeng, Fuxingyong, and speculators bought, pulling the price up by two taels. At 11:10 AM, it was 38 taels and 3 qian, then reduced by seven or eight qian. At 11:30 AM, Chenfengyong, Yuanmaoyong, and others continued to buy, and because the Guangdong Gang was scrambling for exchange bills, the banks' attitude became firm, calculating English gold settling at 375, with the state suddenly looking good. It has now risen by more than two taels. At 11:45 AM, it was 39 taels and 8 qian, briefly reaching 40 taels. Later, buyers stopped and retail investors sold, pushing it down by one and a half taels. At noon, it was 38 taels and 3 qian, then increased to 9 qian. Until the afternoon close, it was 38 taels and a half, a rebound of six taels and a half compared to the previous day, which was a reaction to three consecutive days of decline. The highest price in the half-day was 4 taels and 5 qian, and the lowest price was 36 taels and a half, a range of four taels. The morning price for bullion was 8 taels and 3 qian, and the afternoon close was 8 taels. The announced price was still 777 taels, calculated down by 4 taels to over 38 taels, registered at 39 taels, and water supplemented at 37 taels.

Frequent Transactions. As for the transactions of various firms, Hengxing, Fuyu, Yongfeng, Futaiheng, Chenfengyong, Fuxingyong, and Yuanmao, etc., all bought. Tong Taichang, Wanxing, Shunli, Zhifengyong, Qianchangxiang, Tianfengyong, Yuanheng, and Yuantai, etc., all sold. Dadecheng, Yuanmaoyong, Yuhe, Senchangyong, and Yuankangxiang, etc., had mixed buying and selling, in significant amounts. Bullion speculators were buying and selling intermittently. The Guangdong Gang bought two or three hundred bars, the Dalian Gang sold a total of six or seven hundred bars and bought two or three hundred bars. Speculators’ trading volume was limited, it is said.

Securities 172

Bond Prices Rebounded Sharply This Week

Up Five or Six Yuan Compared to Last Week

Total Trading Reached Over 11.6 Million

This week, the prosperity of the local securities market was unprecedented. Except for one day, the weekend, which was a commemorative day for the National Humiliation of May 9th, the market was always extremely prosperous. Tuesday saw the largest trading volume, totaling 29.9 million. Friday was about 24 million, Monday and Wednesday were each over 20 million, and Thursday was relatively flat, with also about 19 million. In total, the trading volume for the five days reached 11,638,500 yuan, exceeding the previous week by over 2.5 million yuan. The 20% debt, the Disarmament Bond, and the 1928 Customs Loan, etc. were particularly prosperous, while other market conditions were quieter. Last week, people were uneasy, and all debts fell sharply. This week, the political situation improved and people were optimistic. In the first two days of the week, demand exceeded supply for all debts, with prices rising about two yuan each day. However, the trend was more peaceful on Wednesday, with prices rising first and then falling, resulting in no major fluctuations. On Wednesday and Thursday, however, the market rose higher day by day, with each day rising about one yuan. The situation is expected to gradually stabilize from now on. As a result, the 1928 Customs Loan and the 20% debt rebounded by five or six yuan compared to last week. The Disarmament Bond and the Disbandment debt and Whole Six debt also rose by about four yuan, and even the 1896 debt rebounded by about one and a half yuan.
